Shuf'ah Requires Financial Consideration
Ruling that shuf'ah requires a financial consideration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for shuf'ah to be established and distinguish between fungible and non-fungible considerations when determining what the pre-emptor must pay.

Core Idea
No financial consideration means no shuf'ah.

Shuf'ah (pre-emption) gives a co-owner the right to purchase a sold share. But this right only arises when the buyer paid a financial consideration for the property. Why? Because the pre-emptor must step into the buyer's shoes and pay exactly what the buyer paid—or its equivalent. In this lesson, we unpack Imam al-Quduri's ruling that shuf'ah is wajib only when property is acquired by exchange of wealth, and we see how the type of consideration (fungible vs. non-fungible) affects what the pre-emptor must give.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Find the main ruling: shuf'ah becomes wajib (obligatory) when real estate is owned by a consideration that is wealth (mal). This is the core legal statement.
The ruling is conditional: if the buyer gave wealth, then shuf'ah applies; if not, it doesn't.
2
Understand the Shari'ah condition behind the ruling
The text says the condition of the Shari'ah is 'ownership by the equivalent of what the buyer owned.' This means the pre-emptor must replicate the buyer's payment—either the same thing (if fungible) or its value (if non-fungible).
This condition ensures justice: the seller gets the same price, the buyer recovers what he paid.
3
Distinguish the two types of consideration
If the consideration is of the type 'dhawat al-amthal' (fungibles, like wheat or money), the equivalent is an identical item of the same quantity. If it is 'dhawat al-qim' (non-fungibles, like a unique house or jewel), the equivalent is its market value.
This distinction is crucial for correct application.
4
Apply the condition to cases without financial consideration
If the buyer acquired the property by gift, inheritance, or any exchange that does not involve financial consideration, the condition fails and no shuf'ah arises.
This is the practical takeaway: shuf'ah is tied to sales and similar financial exchanges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا ملك العقار بعوض هو مال وجبت فيه الشفعة لانه امكن مراعاة شرط الشرع فيه وهو التملك بثمل ما تملک به المشترى صورة او قيمة على مامر.
ترجمہ امام قدوری نے کہا اور جب مشتری زمین کا مالک بنا ایسے عوض کے ساتھ جو مال ہے تو اس زمین میں شفعہ ثابت ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ اس میں شریعت کی شرط کی رعایت ممکن ہے اور وہ مالک ہونا ہے اسی چیز کے مثل کے بدلہ جس کے ذریعہ مشتری مالک ہوا ہے وہ مثل صورت کے اعتبار سے ہو یا قیمت کے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو گذر گئی۔ تشریح شفعہ بیع سے ثابت ہوتا ہے لہذا بیع ہونی چاہئے یا ایسی چیز کہ جس میں زمین کے بدلے میں مالی معاوضہ دیا گیا ہو ورنہ شفعہ ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہاں شریعت نے یہ شرط لگائی ہے کہ مشتری جس مال کے بدلہ مالک بنا ہے شفیع بھی اس کا مثل ادا کر کے اس کا مالک بنے گا۔ وہ دوسری بات ہے کہ پھر مثل میں تعیم ہے اگر وہ عوض ذوات القیم میں سے ہے تو اس عوض کا مثل اس کی قیمت ہوگی۔ اور اگر ذوات الامثال میں سے ہے تو اس کا مثل اس جیسی وہ چیز ہے جو عرفاً اس کے مثل شمار کی جاتی ہے ورنہ اگر مشتری بغیر عوض مالی کے مالک بن جائے تو شرط نہیں پائی گئی لہذا شفعہ جاری نہیں ہوگا۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And when one owns real estate with a consideration that is wealth, pre-emption becomes obligatory because it is possible to observe the condition of the Shari'ah, which is ownership by the equivalent of what the buyer owned, in form or value, as previously discussed. Translation: Imam Quduri said: When a buyer becomes owner of land with a consideration that is wealth, pre-emption will be established in that land. This is because the condition of the Shari'ah can be observed: that the pre-emptor becomes owner by giving the equivalent of what the buyer gave, either in kind or value, according to the details that have passed. Explanation: Pre-emption is established from sale, so there must be a sale or something in which a financial consideration is given for the land; otherwise pre-emption will not be established. Because the Shari'ah has set the condition that the pre-emptor will give the equivalent of what the buyer gave. Then the equivalent may be specific: if the consideration is of the type valued by estimation (dhawat al-qim), then its equivalent is its value; if it is of the type with standard equivalents (dhawat al-amthal), then its equivalent is a similar item customarily considered equivalent. Conversely, if the buyer becomes owner without financial consideration, the condition is not met, so pre-emption does not apply.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage establishes a fundamental condition for shuf'ah: the buyer must have acquired the property in exchange for 'iwad that is mal (wealth). This is because the pre-emptor (shafi') must pay the equivalent of what the buyer paid. This condition ensures that the transaction can be replicated. The commentary distinguishes between two types of equivalents: if the consideration is a fungible (dhawat al-amthal), like wheat, the pre-emptor gives the same kind; if it is a non-fungible valued by estimation (dhawat al-qim), like a unique painting, the pre-emptor pays its market value. If the buyer acquired the property without paying wealth (e.g., by gift, inheritance), there is no shuf'ah because there is no financial consideration to match.

Key Terms
عوض ('iwad): Consideration given in exchange for property; must be wealth (mal) for shuf'ah to apply.
مثل (mithl): Equivalent; either same kind (mithl suwari) or value (mithl qimi) depending on the type of consideration.
ذوات القیم (dhawat al-qim): Things valued by estimation because they lack standard equivalents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is shuf'ah not established when a person acquires land through a gift (hiba)?
A) Because gifts are invalid for land
B) Because there is no financial consideration to match for the pre-emptor
C) Because the pre-emptor may not want the land
D) Because the donor must consent

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah only binds when the buyer paid a financial consideration; the pre-emptor must pay its equivalent.

Five Cases Where Shuf'ah Is Not Established
Listing of exceptions to shuf'ah based on lack of wealth exchange

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five transactions where shuf'ah does not apply and explain the common reason: absence of exchange of wealth for wealth.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah requires exchange of wealth for wealth; gifts, dowries, and compensations not in wealth do not grant pre-emption.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, al-Quduri lists five specific transactions where the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) does not arise. The key is understanding what constitutes a valid 'exchange of wealth' in the Hanafi view. We will parse each case to see why the consideration is not wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching principle
Recognize that shuf'ah is only established in mubadalah al-mal bil mal (exchange of wealth for wealth). The text states: 'Al-shuf'ah ʻindana innama tajibu fi mubadalah al-mal bil mal.'
If the consideration is not mal (wealth), shuf'ah does not apply.
2
List the five cases
Enumerate the five transactions: (1) mahr (dower), (2) khul' (divorce for compensation), (3) ijarah (lease), (4) sulh ʻan dam ʻamd (settlement for intentional killing), (5) ʻitq (emancipation).
These are the exceptions mentioned by al-Quduri.
3
Analyze the consideration in each case
For each, identify what is given as consideration. For mahr: the husband gives a house in exchange for the right to marital intimacy (bidʻ muhtaram). For khul': the wife gives a house to be released from the marriage. For ijarah: the house is given for usufruct (manfaʻah). For sulh: the house is given to drop the claim for blood. For ʻitq: the house is given for freeing a slave.
None of these considerations are mal mutaqawwim (negotiable wealth).
4
Apply the principle
Because the consideration is not wealth, the condition of mubadalah al-mal bil mal is missing. Therefore, the transaction does not trigger shuf'ah.
The pre-emptor cannot demand the property because he cannot pay the equivalent (since the original consideration is not wealth).
5
Note the practical consequence
The absence of shuf'ah means the neighbor cannot intervene to buy the property from the new owner. The transaction stands without pre-emption.
This is a specific Hanafi ruling; other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کن دیار میں شفعہ کا حق حاصل نہیں ہوتا
قال ولا شفعة فى الدار التى يتزوج الرجل عليها او يخالع المراة بها او يستاجر بها دار اوغيرها او يصالح بها عن دم عمدا ويعتق عليها عبد الآن الشفعة عندنا انما تجب في مبادلة المال بالمال لما بينا وهذه عواض ليست بأموال فايجاب الشفعة فيها خلاف المشروع وقلب الموضوع
ترجمہ اہم قدوری نے کہا اور اس گھر میں شفعہ نہیں ہے جس پر مرد نکاح کرتا ہے یا جس کے ذریعہ عورت ضلع کرتی ہے یا جس کے ذریعہ مردگھر یا اس کے علاوہ کو اجارہ پر لیتا ہے یا جس کے ذریعہ دم عمد سے مصالحت کرتا ہے یا جس کے اوپر غلام کو آزاد کرتا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ شفعہ ہمارے نزدیک مبادلتہ المال بالمال کی صورت میں ثابت ہوتا ہے میں دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور یہ اعواض اموال نہیں ہیں تو ان کے اندر شفعہ ثابت کرنا خلاف مشروع اور قلب موضوع ہو گا۔ تشریح ماقبل میں پہلے مسئلہ میں یہ اصول گذر چکا ہے کہ جہاں مال کا تبادلہ مال کے ساتھ ہو گا وہیں شفعہ ملے گا تاکہ شفیع مثل صوری یا مثل قیمی دے سکے اور جہاں مبادلتہ المال بالمال نہیں پایا جائے گا وہاں شفعہ نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اس کے اندر موضوع کو الٹنا اور امر مشروع کی خلاف ورزی لازم آئے گی ۔ کیونکہ شفعہ مشروع ہوا ہے مبادلتہ المال بالمال کے اندر اور شفعہ کی مشروعیت موضوع ہے۔ مبادلۃ المال بالمال کے اندر۔ لہذا قدوری نے یہاں پانچ ایسی جزئیات بیان کیں جن کے اندر مبادلتہ المال بالمال نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔ ایک شخص نے بوقت نکاح مہر میں ایک گھر مقرر کیا تو اس میں شفعہ نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ مکان کا عوض بضع محترم ہے جو مال متقوم نہیں ہے۔ -۲- عورت کسی مکان کے بدلے اپنے شوہر سے خلع کرتی ہے تو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ یہاں بھی مکان کا عوض اپنی بضع کی خلاصی ہے جو مال نہیں ہے۔
In which properties is the right of pre-emption not obtained? He (al-Quduri) said: There is no pre-emption in a house which a man marries with (as mahr), or with which a woman performs khul' from her husband, or with which he rents a house or other, or with which he makes a settlement for intentional killing, or upon which he emancipates a slave. Because pre-emption in our view is only obligatory in the exchange of wealth for wealth, as we have explained, and these considerations are not wealth, so establishing pre-emption in them would be contrary to the Shari'ah and a reversal of the subject matter. Translation: Imam Quduri said: There is no pre-emption in a house which a man marries with, or with which a woman performs khul', or with which a man rents a house or other, or with which he makes a settlement for intentional blood, or upon which he emancipates a slave. Because pre-emption in our view is established only in exchange of wealth for wealth, due to the evidence we have mentioned, and these considerations are not wealth, so establishing pre-emption in them would be contrary to Shari'ah and a reversal of the subject. Explanation: In the previous issue, the principle was established that wherever there is exchange of wealth for wealth, shuf'ah will be given so that the pre-emptor can give the like in form or value. Where there is no exchange of wealth for wealth, no shuf'ah will be given, because it would involve reversing the subject and violating the prescribed matter. For shuf'ah is prescribed in exchange of wealth for wealth, and its prescription is based on exchange of wealth for wealth. Therefore, al-Quduri mentioned here five instances where due to the absence of exchange of wealth for wealth, shuf'ah will not be given: (1) A person specifies a house as mahr at the time of marriage; there is no shuf'ah because the consideration for the house is the respected private part (bid' muhtaram), which is not negotiable wealth (mal mutaqawwim). (2) A woman obtains khul' from her husband in exchange for a house; no shuf'ah because the consideration for the house is the release of her private part, which is not wealth.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah enumerates five cases where shuf'ah (pre-emption) does not apply, despite involving real estate. The common reason is that the consideration ('iwad) given for the property is not wealth (mal). The five cases are: (1) a house given as mahr (dower) in marriage; (2) a house given by a wife to her husband in khul' (divorce for compensation); (3) a house given as rent (ijarah); (4) a house given as settlement (sulh) for intentional killing; (5) a house given in return for manumitting a slave ('itq). In each, the consideration is not wealth: in mahr it is the husband's right to marital intimacy (bid' muhtaram), in khul' it is the wife's release from marriage, in ijarah it is the benefit of a house (not a transfer of wealth), in sulh it is the right to blood (not wealth), and in 'itq it is the benefit of freedom. The text explains that Shari'ah has legislated shuf'ah only in exchange of wealth for wealth (mubadalah al-mal bil mal), because the pre-emptor must be able to pay the equivalent. The OCR cuts off after the second case, but the author intended to list all five.

Key Terms
مبادلة المال بالمال (mubadalah al-mal bil mal): Exchange of wealth for wealth; the essential condition for shuf'ah.
بضع (bid'): The private part; in legal context, the right to sexual intercourse, considered a respected but non-wealth entity.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife who pays compensation to the husband.
عوض ('iwad): Consideration; the thing given in exchange in a contract.
مال متقوم (mal mutaqawwim): Negotiable wealth; property that is permissible to benefit from and has market value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the marriage contract is invalid
D) Because the wife does not own the house

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah in the Hanafi school requires a pure wealth-for-wealth exchange; without it, the right of pre-emption does not arise.

General Principle: Shuf'ah Only with Financial Exchange
Ruling statement establishing the fundamental condition for shuf'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for shuf'ah and apply it to determine whether shuf'ah is established in a given transaction.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah requires financial exchange — no sale, no preemption.

The right of preemption (shuf'ah) is not automatic in every property transfer. Imam Quduri opens the Book of Shuf'ah with a fundamental condition: the buyer must have become owner through a financial consideration (badal mal). This lesson unpacks that condition and its implications for the preemptor's right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction
Look at how the buyer acquired the property. Is it a sale, barter, gift, inheritance, or other?
2
Check for financial consideration
Determine if the buyer gave something of value (mal) in exchange for the property. The consideration can be cash, goods, or any wealth.
Financial consideration is the key; services or mere promises are not sufficient.
3
Determine the equivalent (mithl)
If shuf'ah is established, the preemptor must pay the equivalent of what the buyer paid. For fungibles (mithliyyat), the equivalent is in kind; for non-fungibles (qimiyyat), it is the value.
This distinction affects how the preemptor compensates the buyer.
4
Conclude shuf'ah status
If the buyer paid financial consideration, shuf'ah is established. If not (e.g., gift, inheritance), shuf'ah does not apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ ترجمہ امام قدوری نے کہا اور جب مشتری زمین کا مالک بنا ایسے عوض کے ساتھ جو مال ہے تو اس زمین میں شفعہ ثابت ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ اس میں شریعت کی شرط کی رعایت ممکن ہے اور وہ مالک ہونا ہے اسی چیز کے مثل کے بدلہ جس کے ذریعہ مشتری مالک ہوا ہے وہ مثل صورت کے اعتبار سے ہو یا قیمت کے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو گذر گئی۔ تشریح شفعہ بیع سے ثابت ہوتا ہے لہذا بیع ہونی چاہئے یا ایسی چیز کہ جس میں زمین کے بدلے میں مالی معاوضہ دیا گیا ہو ورنہ شفعہ ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔
کیونکہ یہاں شریعت نے یہ شرط لگائی ہے کہ مشتری جس مال کے بدلہ مالک بنا ہے شفیع بھی اس کا مثل ادا کر کے اس کا مالک بنے گا۔
وہ دوسری بات ہے کہ پھر مثل میں تعیم ہے اگر وہ عوض ذوات القیم میں سے ہے تو اس عوض کا مثل اس کی قیمت ہوگی۔ اور اگر ذوات الامثال میں سے ہے تو اس کا مثل اس جیسی وہ چیز ہے جو عرفاً اس کے مثل شمار کی جاتی ہے ورنہ اگر مشتری بغیر عوض مالی کے مالک بن جائے تو شرط نہیں پائی گئی لہذا شفعہ جاری نہیں ہوگا۔
Book of Shuf'ah. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 13. Imam Quduri said: And when the buyer becomes owner of the land by a consideration that is wealth, then shuf'ah is established in that land. Because in it, observance of the condition of the Shari'ah is possible, and that ownership is by the equivalent of the thing by which the buyer became owner; that equivalent is either in kind (mithl suri) or by value (qimah) according to the detail that has passed. Explanation: Shuf'ah is established by sale, so there must be a sale or something in which financial compensation is given for the land; otherwise shuf'ah will not be established. Because the Shari'ah has put the condition that the shafi' (preemptor) will become owner by paying the equivalent of the wealth by which the buyer became owner. Another matter: then in the equivalent, there is specification: if the consideration is from items of value (dhawat al-qim), then its equivalent is its value; if from items of kind (dhawat al-amthal), then its equivalent is a similar thing that is customarily considered its like. Otherwise, if the buyer becomes owner without financial consideration, the condition is not fulfilled, so shuf'ah will not apply.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Imam Quduri’s matn, explaining the foundational principle of shuf'ah (preemption). The key condition for shuf'ah is that the buyer must have acquired the property in exchange for a financial consideration (badal mal). The preemptor (shafi') gains the right to take the property by paying the equivalent of that consideration. The equivalent is determined either by kind (mithl suri) if the consideration is from fungible items (dhawat al-amthal), or by value (qimah) if it is from non-fungible items (dhawat al-qim). Therefore, shuf'ah is only established in transactions involving financial exchange, such as sale or any contract where monetary compensation is given. If the buyer acquires the property without financial consideration (e.g., gift, inheritance), shuf'ah does not apply. This rule is the foundation for the cases that follow.

Key Terms
شفعہ (shuf'ah): A right of preemption allowing a co-owner or neighbor to purchase property sold to an outsider by paying the consideration.
مثل (mithl): The equivalent of a thing; either in kind (for fungibles) or in value (for non-fungibles).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary condition for shuf'ah to be established?
A) The buyer must be a co-owner
B) The property must be land
C) The buyer acquired the property in exchange for financial consideration
D) The seller must be a neighbor

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah is only established when the buyer acquires property in exchange for financial consideration (badal mal).

Five Cases Where Shuf'ah Is Not Granted
Inter-madhhab dispute on five exceptions to shuf'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five cases where shuf'ah is not granted in the Hanafi school and explain the Hanafi principle of mubadala al-mal bi al-mal.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah requires exchange of wealth for wealth; non-financial considerations block the right.

This passage from the Hidayah presents five specific transactions where the right of preemption (shuf'ah) does not arise in the Hanafi school. The central principle is that shuf'ah only applies when there is an exchange of financial wealth (mal) for financial wealth. The five cases – mahr, khula, ijara, sulh for qisas, and 'itq – all involve considerations that Hanafis classify as non-wealth. We will explore each case, the Shafi'i objection, and the Hanafi rejoinder.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi condition for shuf'ah
Identify the principle: shuf'ah only applies in mubadala al-mal bi al-mal (exchange of wealth for wealth).
2
List the five exceptional cases
Name each case and the non-wealth consideration: (1) mahr – bud', (2) khula – release from marriage, (3) ijara – usufruct, (4) sulh for qisas – qisas, (5) 'itq – freedom.
3
Explain why each consideration is not mal
For each, briefly state why Hanafis do not consider it financial property (e.g., bud' is not traded; usufruct is not owned as property; qisas is a right of retaliation; freedom is not a commodity).
4
Present the Shafi'i counter-argument
Imam al-Shafi'i considers these considerations valuable (mutaqawwim) and analogizes them to sale by goods (bay' bi al-'ard).
5
Note the Hanafi response
Even if they have value in some contexts, that valuation is necessary and does not establish shuf'ah, which is restricted to financial exchanges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کن دیار میں شفعہ کا حق حاصل نہیں ہوتا
قال ولا شفعة فى الدار التى يتزوج الرجل عليها او يخالع المراة بها او يستاجر بها دار اوغيرها او يصالح بها عن دم عمدا ويعتق عليها عبد الآن الشفعة عندنا انما تجب في مبادلة المال بالمال لما بينا وهذه عواض ليست بأموال فايجاب الشفعة فيها خلاف المشروع وقلب الموضوع
ترجمہ اہم قدوری نے کہا اور اس گھر میں شفعہ نہیں ہے جس پر مرد نکاح کرتا ہے یا جس کے ذریعہ عورت ضلع کرتی ہے یا جس کے ذریعہ مردگھر یا اس کے علاوہ کو اجارہ پر لیتا ہے یا جس کے ذریعہ دم عمد سے مصالحت کرتا ہے یا جس کے اوپر غلام کو آزاد کرتا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ شفعہ ہمارے نزدیک مبادلتہ المال بالمال کی صورت میں ثابت ہوتا ہے میں دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور یہ اعواض اموال نہیں ہیں تو ان کے اندر شفعہ ثابت کرنا خلاف مشروع اور قلب موضوع ہو گا۔ تشریح ماقبل میں پہلے مسئلہ میں یہ اصول گذر چکا ہے کہ جہاں مال کا تبادلہ مال کے ساتھ ہو گا وہیں شفعہ ملے گا تاکہ شفیع مثل صوری یا مثل قیمی دے سکے اور جہاں مبادلتہ المال بالمال نہیں پایا جائے گا وہاں شفعہ نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اس کے اندر موضوع کو الٹنا اور امر مشروع کی خلاف ورزی لازم آئے گی ۔
کیونکہ شفعہ مشروع ہوا ہے مبادلتہ المال بالمال کے اندر اور شفعہ کی مشروعیت موضوع ہے۔ مبادلۃ المال بالمال کے اندر۔ لہذا
قدوری نے یہاں پانچ ایسی جزئیات بیان کیں جن کے اندر مبادلتہ المال بالمال نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔ ایک شخص نے بوقت نکاح مہر میں ایک گھر مقرر کیا تو اس میں شفعہ نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ مکان کا عوض بضع محترم ہے جو مال متقوم
نہیں ہے۔
-۲- عورت کسی مکان کے بدلے اپنے شوہر سے خلع کرتی ہے تو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ یہاں بھی مکان کا عوض اپنی بضع کی خلاصی ہے جو
مال نہیں ہے۔
کسی نے اپنے مکان کے بدلے کوئی مکان یا کوئی اور چیز کرایہ پر لی تو اس صورت میں شفعہ نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ مکان یا کسی اور چیز کے
منافع مال نہیں ہیں ۔
کسی پر قصاص واجب تھا اس نے مقتول کے وارثین سے کسی مکان کے بدلے میں مصالحت کر لی تو شفعہ نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ قصاص مال
نہیں ہے۔
۔ کسی نے اپنے غلام سے کہا کہ فلاں مکان مجھے دے دے اور تو آزاد ہے اس نے وہ مکان دے دیا تو اس میں شفعہ نہیں ہوگا اسلئے کہ
آزادی مال نہیں ہے۔
مذکورہ دیار میں امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
وعند الشافعي تجب فيها الشفعة لان هذه الاعواض متقومة عنده فامكن الاخذ بقيمتها ان تعذر بمثلها کمافى البيع بالعرض بخلاف الهبة لانه لا عوض فيها راسا وقوله يتاتى فيما اذا جعل شقصا من دار مهرا او ما يضاهبه لانه لاشفعة عنده الافيه
ترجمہ اور شافعی کے نزدیک ان میں شفعہ ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ ان کے نزدیک یہ اعواض قیمتی ہیں تو ان کی قیمت لینا ممکن ہو گا۔ اگر ان کے مثل کو کر لینا مستعد رہو جائے جیسے سامان کے بدلے بیج کے اندر بخلاف ہبہ کے اس لئے کہ اسکے اندر بالکل عوض نہیں اور اکتشافعی کا یہ قول فٹ بیٹھے گا۔ اس صورت میں جبکہ شوہر نے کر دیا ہو گھر کا کچھ حصہ مہر یا اس کے مشابہ اسلئے کہ شفعہ نہیں ہے ان کے
نزدیک مگر اس میں ۔ تشریح حنفیہ نے مذکورہ چیزوں کو قیمتی مال نہیں سمجھا اسلئے شفعہ کا انکار کر دیا اور امام شافعی نے ان کو مال متقوم سمجھا اسلئے کہ وہ تمام چیزوں کے اندر شفعہ کے قائل ہیں اور فرماتے ہیں جس طرح سامان کے بدلہ بیع کی صورت میں مثل صوری کے بجائے قیمت واجب
ہوتی ہے۔
اسی طرح ان اشیاء کے اندر اگر مشل حعذر ہے تو قیمت تو واجب کی جاسکتی ہے۔ لہذا بیج با العرض کے مثل ان میں بھی شفعہ ثابت ہوگا ہاں اگر کسی نے کسی کو کوئی مکان ہبہ کر دیا تو اس میں امام شافعی کے نزدیک بھی شفعہ نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس میں بالکلیہ عوض ہے نہیں کہ اس کے تقوم و عدم تقوم سے بحث کی جائے۔ ما قبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک فقط شریک کوشفعہ ملتا ہے تو ان کے یہاں یہ مثال اس وقت درست ہوگی کہ مثلا شو ہر کا ایک مشترک مکان ہے اس نے اپنا حصہ مہر میں دے دیا یا کسی اور چیز کے عوض دے دیا تو دوسرے شریک کو اس میں شفعہ ملے گا ۔ ورنہ اگر شوہر نے اپنا پورا مملوک مکان مہر میں دیا ہو تو چونکہ اس میں کسی کی شرکت نہیں ہے لہذا امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس میں شفعہ نہ ہوگا۔ اسی کو صاحب ہدایہ نے وقوله يتاتی ... الخ سے بیان کیا ہے۔
امام شافعی کے مستدلات کے جوابات
ونحن نقول ان تقوم منافع البضع في النكاح وغيرها بعقد الاجارة ضرورى فلا يظهر في حق الشفعة وكذا
In which dwellings the right of shuf'ah is not acquired. He said: There is no shuf'ah in the house upon which a man marries, or by which a woman divorces (khula'), or by which a house or other is rented, or by which settlement is made for intentional killing, or upon which a slave is freed. Because shuf'ah according to us is only obligatory in exchange of wealth for wealth, as we have explained, and these considerations are not wealth, so making shuf'ah obligatory in them is contrary to the Shar' and a reversal of the subject. Translation of Imam Quduri: He said: In a house for which a man marries, or by which a woman does khula', or by which a man rents a house or other, or by which he makes settlement for intentional killing, or upon which he frees a slave, there is no shuf'ah. Because shuf'ah according to us is established only in exchange of wealth for wealth due to the evidence we have stated, and these considerations are not wealth, so making shuf'ah established in them would be contrary to the Shar' and a reversal of the subject. Explanation: In the previous issue, the principle has passed that wherever there is exchange of wealth for wealth, there shuf'ah will be granted, so that the shafi' can pay the equivalent in kind or value. And where there is no exchange of wealth for wealth, there shuf'ah will not be granted, because it would entail reversing the subject and violating the Shar'. Because shuf'ah is legislated in exchange of wealth for wealth, and the legislation of shuf'ah is subject to exchange of wealth for wealth. Hence, Quduri mentioned five such cases in which, due to the absence of exchange of wealth for wealth, shuf'ah will not be granted: 1. A person sets a house as mahr at the time of marriage – no shuf'ah because the consideration for the house is the respected private part (bud'), which is not valuable property. 2. A woman makes khula' with her husband in exchange for a house – no shuf'ah because here the consideration is the release of her private part, which is not property. 3. A person rents a house or other thing in exchange for his house – no shuf'ah because the usufruct (manafi') of a house or anything else is not property. 4. A person had qisas obligatory upon him and he settled with the heirs of the deceased in exchange for a house – no shuf'ah because qisas is not property. 5. A person said to his slave: 'Give me such-and-such house and you are free.' The slave gave the house – no shuf'ah because freedom is not property. The viewpoint of Imam Shafi'i regarding the mentioned dwellings: And according to Shafi'i, shuf'ah is obligatory in them because these considerations according to him are valuable (mutaqawwim), so it is possible to take their value if their like is unavailable, just as in sale by exchange of goods ('ard), as opposed to gift (hiba) because there is no consideration at all. And his statement applies when a person makes a share of a house as mahr or its like, because there is no shuf'ah according to him except in it. Translation: And according to Shafi'i, shuf'ah is established in these, because these considerations according to him are valuable, so taking their value is possible if their like is difficult, just as in sale by goods. Unlike gift, because there is no consideration at all. And his statement fits when the husband gives a portion of a house as mahr or similar, because there is no shuf'ah according to him except in it. Explanation: The Hanafis did not consider the mentioned things valuable property, so they denied shuf'ah. Imam Shafi'i considered them valuable property, so he affirms shuf'ah in all of them, saying: Just as in a sale by goods, when the like is impossible, value becomes obligatory; similarly in these cases, if the like is absent, value can be made obligatory. So like sale by goods, shuf'ah will be established in these. Yes, if someone gives a house as a gift (hiba), then according to Shafi'i there is no shuf'ah, because there is absolutely no consideration to discuss its valuableness or non-valuableness. It has passed before that according to Shafi'i, only a co-owner gets shuf'ah, so this example would be correct when, for example, the husband has a shared house and gives his share as mahr or in exchange for something else, then the other partner will get shuf'ah in it. Otherwise, if the husband gives his entire privately owned house as mahr, since there is no partnership, there would be no shuf'ah according to Shafi'i. The author of Hidayah has expressed this with his statement 'and his statement applies...'. The rejoinder to Imam Shafi'i's proofs: And we say: The valuation of the benefits of the private part in marriage and others through a contract of hire (ijara) is necessary, so it does not appear in the right of shuf'ah, and likewise...
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage presents five specific cases where shuf'ah is not granted according to the Hanafi school, followed by the Shafi'i opinion and the Hanafi rejoinder. The overarching principle is that shuf'ah only applies in exchanges of wealth for wealth (mubadala al-mal bi al-mal). The five cases are: marriage (mahr), khula' (divorce by compensation), rental (ijara), settlement for intentional homicide (sulh 'an dam 'amd), and manumission for property ('itq 'ala mal). In each, the consideration is not considered 'mal' (wealth) in the Hanafi view: the private part (bud'), the release from marriage, usufruct, retaliation (qisas), and freedom are not property. Therefore, shuf'ah does not arise. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, considering these considerations as valuable property (mutaqawwim), so he grants shuf'ah by analogy to sale by goods (bay' bi al-'ard). The Hanafi response argues that even if these benefits have value in some contexts (like hiring), that valuation is necessary (daruri) and not sufficient to establish shuf'ah. The text notes that Shafi'i's shuf'ah only applies to co-owners (shuraka'), so his ruling is limited to cases where the property is shared.

Key Terms
مبادلتہ المال بالمال (mubadala al-mal bi al-mal): Exchange of wealth for wealth; a condition for shuf'ah in the Hanafi school.
بضع (bud'): Female private parts; considered not property in the context of mahr.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation for murder; not property.
خلع (khula'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation to the husband.
اجارہ (ijara): Lease or rental contract; the consideration is usufruct (manafi').
عتیق ('itq): Manumission of a slave; freedom is not property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the five cases where shuf'ah is not granted according to Hanafis?
A) A house given as mahr in marriage
B) A house given in exchange for khula'
C) A house sold for a price
D) A house given to settle for qisas

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah in the Hanafi school is strictly limited to exchanges of wealth for wealth; non-financial considerations like marriage, divorce, or freedom do not trigger the right of preemption.

Compromise and Preemption: When Sulh Creates Shuf'ah Rights
Ruling with proof: conditions for shuf'ah in sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a compromise (sulh) on a house establishes the right of preemption (shuf'ah), distinguishing between compromise with acknowledgment, denial, and silence.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, preemption arises from compromise only when the defendant acknowledges the claimant's ownership; denial or silence prevents shuf'ah.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced question: when does a compromise settlement (sulh) over a disputed house create a right of preemption (shuf'ah) for a third party? The answer depends on the mindset of the defendant—whether he acknowledges the claimant's ownership, denies it, or remains silent. The text, expanding on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, clarifies that only a compromise with acknowledgment constitutes a true sale, thereby triggering shuf'ah. We will walk through the reasoning and the intra-Hanafi correction that leads to the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
Recognize that a third party claims shuf'ah after a dispute over a house was settled by compromise (sulh) between claimant and defendant. The compromise may occur with the defendant's acknowledgment (iqrar), denial (inkar), or silence (sukut).
The house is the subject of both the dispute and the compromise.
2
State al-Quduri's original ruling
Al-Quduri wrote that if a person compromises regarding the house with denial, but then if he compromises with acknowledgment, shuf'ah becomes obligatory. The wording 'regarding it' (alayha) caused ambiguity.
Most copies of al-Mukhtasar carry this wording.
3
Analyze al-Marghinani's correction
The author of al-Hidayah corrects the text to 'with denial' (bi-inkar) instead of 'regarding it', explaining that compromise with denial or silence does not transfer ownership—the defendant still believes the house is his. The payment is seen as ransom for his oath or to halt the opponent's harassment.
The correction sharpens the distinction between acknowledgment and non-acknowledgment.
4
Understand the rationale
With acknowledgment, the defendant admits the claimant's ownership and then buys the house via compromise—this is a true sale (mubadala mali). With denial or silence, no sale occurs because the defendant does not treat the payment as purchase price; thus shuf'ah does not arise.
The key is the defendant's belief about ownership, not the external form of payment.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that shuf'ah is NOT established with denial or silence. Only compromise with acknowledgment triggers shuf'ah. This is the corrected view of al-Marghinani.
Some later texts mention an alternative view that shuf'ah applies in all three, but the correct position is as above.

کر اس نے مصالحت کی ہے شفعہ کا دعویٰ کر دیا۔ سوال اب سوال یہ ہے کہ ناظم کو شفعہ ملے گا یا نہیں؟ جواب تو یہاں اس کا جواب دیا گیا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اس کا مدار مصالحت کی کیفیت پر ہے، جس کی تین صورتیں ہیں :۔ عدنان نے اقرار کیا ہو کہ ہاں مکان مطیع الرحمن کا ہے اور پھر ہزار روپے میں مصالحت کر لی ہو تو اس صورت میں ناظم کو شفعہ ملے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ کھلی ہوئی بیع ہے اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ ملک مدعی کی تھی۔ مدعلی علیہ نے ہزار روپے کے بدلے ملک کو حاصل کیا ہے۔ - عدنان نے مدعی کی ملکیت کا انکار کیا مگر پھر بھی جھگڑے کا شر دور کرنے کیلئے ہزار روپے دے کر مصالحت کر لی ہو تو اب شفعہ ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ عدنان یوں کہتا ہے کہ اس گھر کا برابر میں ہی مالک چلا آرہا ہوں تو بیع کے معنی نہیں پائے گئے ۔ - عدنان نے اس کی ملکیت کا نہ اقرار کیا اور نہ انکار کیا تو اب بھی شفعہ نہ ہو گا۔ اسلئے کہ اس میں احتمال ہے کہ اس نے ہزار روپے اسلئے دیئے ہوں کہ اگر مدعی گواہ پیش نہ کر سکا تو مجھے قسم کھانی پڑے گی اور شریف لوگ حتی الوسع قسم کھانے سے گریز کیا کرتے ہیں۔ اگر چہ سچی ہی قسم کیوں نہ ہو۔ اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ اس نے جھگڑا ختم کرنے کیلئے ہزار روپے دے دیئے ہوں۔ کیونکہ شریف لوگ جھگڑے سے حتی الوسع گریز کیا کرتے ہیں۔ بہر حال اس کے ہزار روپے دے کر مصالحت کرنا اس بات کی دلیل نہیں ہے کہ اس نے مدعی کی ملکیت کا اقرار کر لیا تو یہ انکار کے درجہ میں رہے گا اور شفعہ ثابت نہ ہوگا ۔ مسئلہ پورا ہو گیا۔
Whether he makes a compromise with denial or with acknowledgment, in which does the right of preemption exist? He said: 'Or he makes a compromise with denial regarding it. For if he makes a compromise with acknowledgment regarding it, preemption becomes obligatory.' The author (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'Thus it is mentioned in most copies of al-Mukhtasar, and the correct is: “or he makes a compromise with denial regarding it” in place of his saying “regarding it”. Because when he makes a compromise with denial regarding it, the house remains in his hand, and he claims that it has not left his ownership. Similarly, when he makes a compromise with silence regarding it, because it is possible that he spent the money as a ransom for his oath and to stop the disturbance of his opponent, just as when he explicitly denied. Contrary to when he makes a compromise with acknowledgment regarding it, because he acknowledges the ownership of the claimant, and he only obtained this ownership through the compromise, so it is a financial exchange. But when he makes a compromise with acknowledgment or silence or denial, preemption is obligatory in all these cases because he took it as a substitute for his right in his claim when it is not of the same type as his right, so he is treated according to his claim.' Translation: Al-Quduri said: 'He made a compromise regarding the house with denial. If he makes a compromise regarding the house with acknowledgment, preemption is established.' The author says that in most copies of al-Mukhtasar it is mentioned thus, and the correct is: 'or he makes a compromise with denial regarding it' instead of his saying 'regarding it'. Because when he makes a compromise regarding the house with denial, the house remains in his possession, and he claims that the house has not left his ownership. Similarly, when he makes a compromise regarding the house with silence, because it is possible that he spent the money as ransom for his oath and to end the disturbance of his opponent, just as when he explicitly denied. Contrary to the case when he makes a compromise regarding the house with acknowledgment, because he acknowledges ownership for the claimant, and he has obtained this ownership through compromise, so it is a financial exchange. Nevertheless, when he makes a compromise with acknowledgment or silence or denial, in all these cases preemption is established because he took the house as a substitute for his right according to his claim, when it is not of the same type as his right, so he is treated according to his claim. Explanation: Muti' al-Rahman claimed against Adnan: 'The house in which Adnan resides is mine; he is wrongfully occupying it.' Adnan, to avoid dispute, gave one thousand rupees to Muti' al-Rahman and made a compromise, and both were satisfied, and the dispute ended. Now Nazim claimed preemption in this house in which Adnan resides and concerning which he made a compromise by giving one thousand rupees. Question: Now the question is: Will Nazim get preemption or not? Answer: Here the answer is given. The summary is that it depends on the nature of the compromise, which has three scenarios: (1) Adnan acknowledged that the house belongs to Muti' al-Rahman and then made a compromise for one thousand rupees: in this case, Nazim will get preemption because it is an open sale, and it is clear that the property belonged to the claimant, and the defendant obtained the property in exchange for one thousand rupees. (2) Adnan denied the claimant's ownership but still gave one thousand rupees and made a compromise to end the dispute: then preemption will not be established because Adnan says that he himself has always been the owner of the house, so the meaning of sale is not found. (3) Adnan neither acknowledged nor denied the claimant's ownership: then also preemption will not occur because there is a possibility that he gave the one thousand rupees because if the claimant could not produce witnesses, he would have to take an oath, and noble people avoid oaths as much as possible, even if it is a true oath. Also there is a possibility that he gave the one thousand rupees to end the dispute, because noble people avoid disputes as much as possible. Nevertheless, his giving one thousand rupees and making a compromise is not evidence that he acknowledged the claimant's ownership; thus it remains in the category of denial, and preemption will not be established. The issue is complete.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that determines when preemption (shuf'ah) applies to a house that has been the subject of a compromise (sulh) between a claimant and a defendant. The text begins by quoting al-Quduri's statement that if a person makes a compromise concerning a house while denying the claimant's right, and then if he makes a compromise with acknowledgment, preemption becomes obligatory. The author of al-Hidayah, Imam al-Marghinani (here referred to as 'radi allahu anhu'), clarifies that the correct wording is 'with denial' (bi-inkar) instead of 'concerning it' (alayha). The reasoning is that when one compromises with denial, the house remains in his possession and he believes it is still his property; similarly, if he compromises with silence (sukut), it is as if he is paying off the opponent's disturbance or avoiding an oath. In contrast, if he acknowledges the claimant's ownership and then compromises, the transaction is a genuine financial exchange (mubadala mali), so shuf'ah applies. However, the author then notes that according to the relied-upon position, shuf'ah is established in all three cases (with acknowledgment, silence, or denial) because the person taking the house views it as compensation for his claimed right, and if the compensation is not of the same type as his right, he is judged according to his claim. The explanation provides a concrete example: Muti' al-Rahman claims Adnan's house; Adnan either acknowledges, denies, or remains silent. Only when Adnan acknowledges does the transaction become a true sale, allowing a third-party neighbor (Nazim) to claim shuf'ah. In the other two scenarios, the payment is seen as a ransom for oath or dispute avoidance, not a sale, so no shuf'ah. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that the intention and acknowledgment behind a transaction determine its legal nature.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): Compromise: an agreement to settle a dispute by mutual concession, often involving payment.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment: the defendant admits the claimant's right.
انکار (inkar): Denial: the defendant rejects the claimant's claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hidayah, when does a compromise (sulh) on a house give rise to a right of preemption (shuf'ah)?
A) Only when the compromise is with acknowledgment
B) Only when the compromise is with denial
C) In all cases, whether with acknowledgment, denial, or silence
D) Only when the defendant remains silent

Key Takeaway
A compromise triggers shuf'ah only if the defendant acknowledges the claimant's ownership; denial or silence makes the payment a non-sale and shuf'ah does not arise.

Shuf'ah in Compromise for a Different Disputed Property
Ruling on shuf'ah in a compromise for a different property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios in which shuf'ah does or does not apply in a compromise transaction and explain the role of the recipient's belief.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah in a compromise depends on whether the property given is compensation for a different right.

In this passage, we examine a nuanced ruling from al-Hidayah about preemption (shuf'ah) when a house is given as a compromise to settle a dispute over another item. The key is identifying whether the transaction is a financial exchange (sale) or a mere recognition of possession. The ruling turns on the subject of the original dispute and the subjective belief of the recipient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the dispute
The scenario involves Zaid and Amr. Amr is in possession of an item disputed by Zaid. Amr compromises by giving his own house to Zaid. Determine what the original dispute is about.
The passage assumes two possibilities: the dispute is about something other than the house, or it is about the house itself.
2
Classify the compromise
If the original dispute is about a different property, the house given is a substitute for Zaid's right, making the transaction a financial exchange (mubadala mali). If the dispute is about the house itself, the compromise merely transfers possession, not a sale.
A financial exchange triggers shuf'ah; a mere possession transfer does not.
3
Apply the principle of belief (guman)
The establishment of shuf'ah also depends on Zaid's belief: if Zaid considers the house as compensation for a right of a different type (i.e., not the house itself), then it is a sale-like exchange and shuf'ah applies. Otherwise, it does not.
The Hanafi school gives weight to subjective intention in determining the nature of a transaction.
4
State the ruling for each scenario
Scenario 1: Dispute about a different property → shuf'ah is established. Scenario 2: Dispute about the house itself → no shuf'ah.
This is the mufta bihi position from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرا مسئلہ زید اور عمرو کا کسی چیز کے متعلق جھگڑا ہے۔ زید کہتا ہے میری چیز ہے اور عمر و اس پر قابض ہے اب عمرو نے زید سے مصالحت کر لی اور مصالحت میں زید کو اپنا گھر دے دیا تو اب اس گھر میں شفعہ ہوگا یا نہیں ؟ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ یہاں پر دو صورتیں ہیں۔ جھگڑا کسی اور چیز کے بارے میں ہے اور مصالحت گھر دے کر کی ہو تو ظاہر ہے کہ یہ گھر زید کے حق کا عوض ہے تو مبادلہ مالی پایا گیا لہذا شفعہ ثابت ہوگا۔ -۲- اس گھر کے بارے میں جھگڑا ہے تو عمرو نے اس کو وہ گھر دے کر مصالحت کر لی تو اب بیج کے معنی نہیں پائے گئے ۔ لہذا شفعہ نہ ہوگا۔ حاصل کلام یہاں شفعہ کے ثبوت کا مدار زید کے گمان پر ہے اگر وہ مکان کو اپنے حق کی جنس میں سے نہ سمجھے تو شفعہ ہے ورنہ نہیں ہے۔ دوسرا مسئلہ ختم ہوا۔
Second issue: There is a dispute between Zaid and Amr concerning some thing. Zaid says it is my thing and Amr is in possession of it. Now Amr made a compromise with Zaid and gave his own house in the compromise. So will there be preemption in this house or not? The answer given is that there are two scenarios: (1) The dispute is about some other thing and the compromise was made by giving the house. Then it is obvious that this house is the substitute for Zaid's right, so a financial exchange is found, hence preemption will be established. (2) The dispute is about this house itself, and Amr made a compromise by giving that same house. Then the meaning of sale is not found, so preemption will not occur. The conclusion: Here the establishment of preemption depends on Zaid's belief; if he considers the house not to be of the same type as his right, then there is preemption, otherwise not. The second issue is complete.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a ruling without explicit proof, presenting a second mas'ala regarding shuf'ah in a compromise context. The scenario involves a dispute between Zaid and Amr over an item (not specified). Amr, who is in possession, compromises by giving his own house to Zaid. The question is whether a third party can claim shuf'ah in that house. The author distinguishes two cases: first, if the original dispute is about a different property (not the house), then the house given in compromise is a genuine substitute for Zaid's right, making the transaction a financial exchange (mubadala mali), and thus shuf'ah is established. Second, if the dispute is about the house itself, and Amr gives that same house to Zaid as a compromise, then it is not a sale but rather a surrender of possession, so no shuf'ah. The overarching principle is that shuf'ah hinges on the perception of the parties: if Zaid views the house as compensation for a right of a different type (i.e., not the house), it is a financial exchange; if he views it as the same property in dispute, it is not. This demonstrates the Hanafi rule that shuf'ah applies to compensatory exchanges where the subject matter is considered a commodity (mubadala mali), not to mere settlement of possession.

Key Terms
گمان (guman): Belief or perception: the subjective view of the person receiving the house in compromise determines the nature of the transaction.
شفعہ (shuf'ah): Preemption: the right of a co-owner or neighbour to purchase a sold property by paying its price, preventing a stranger from acquiring it.
مصالحت (musalahat): Compromise or settlement: an agreement to end a dispute by mutual concession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second mas'ala, if the dispute is about a horse, and Amr gives his house as compromise, does shuf'ah apply?
A) Yes, because the house is given for a different right
B) No, because the house is not the disputed item
C) Maybe, depending on the value
D) No, because shuf'ah only applies to sales

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah in a compromise is established only when the property given is a substitute for a different disputed right, and it hinges on the recipient's belief that it is not the same as the disputed item.

Shuf'ah in Hibah and Hibah bi-Shart al-'Iwad
Ruling on shuf'ah in hibah and conditional hibah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shuf'ah in pure hibah vs hibah bi-shart al-'iwad and explain the reasoning based on the dual nature of the contract.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah applies to hibah bi-shart al-'iwad because it is a sale in its finality, not a pure gift.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies a critical distinction: a pure gift does not trigger shuf'ah, but a gift with a condition of compensation does. The reasoning hinges on how the law classifies the contract's inception (ibtida') versus its culmination (intiha'). Let's unpack the logic.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two contract types
Identify pure hibah (no compensation) and hibah bi-shart al-'iwad (compensation stipulated). The ruling differs based on this distinction.
Pure hibah lacks financial exchange; conditional hibah includes it.
2
Analyze the dual nature
The conditional gift is a gift at inception (ahkam al-hibah apply) but a sale at completion (ahkam al-bay' apply). This dual nature justifies applying sale rulings like shuf'ah.
The text says 'it is a sale in its finality' (intiha'an).
3
Apply shuf'ah conditions
For shuf'ah to be established, possession (qabd) is required, and both the gifted property and compensation must be divided (not undivided shares). These are conditions from the gift side.
If property or compensation is undivided, shuf'ah is not established.
4
Understand the exception
If compensation is given later without stipulation in the contract, the transaction remains a pure gift; no shuf'ah arises. The compensation only prevents revocation.
This is clarified in the passage: 'each one is an absolute gift'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیہ صالح عنها کا مطلب یہ ہوتا ہے کہ گھر کے بارے میں جھگڑا ہے اور کوئی اور چیز دے کر مصالحت کرلی ہو اور بصالح عليها کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ گھر ہی مصالحت میں دیا ہو تو اس پر صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ قدوری کے اکثر نسخوں میں عبارت او يصالح علیھا ہے۔ حالانکہ او يصالح عنھا ہونی چاہئے ورنہ مسئلہ کی نوعیت بدل جائے گی جیسا کہ ظاہر ہے۔

ہبہ کی ہوئی زمین میں شفعہ کا حق ہے یا نہیں

قال ولا شفعة فى هبة لما ذكرنا الا ان تكون بعوض مشروط لانه بيع انتهاء ولا بد من القبض وان لا يكون الموهوب ولا عوضه شائعا لانه هبة ابتداء وقد قررناه فى كتاب الهبة بخلاف ما اذا لم يكن العوض مشروطاً في العقد لان كل واحد منهما هبة مطلقة الا انه أثبت منها فامتنع الرجوع ترجمہ امام قدوری نے فرمایا اور ہبہ کے اندر شفعہ نہیں ہے۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں ۔ مگر یہ کہ ہبہ مشروط عوض کے ساتھ ہو۔ اسلئے کہ یہ انتہا کے اعتبار سے بیج ہے اور ضروری ہے قبضہ کا ہونا اور یہ کہ موہوب اور اس کا عوض شائع (غیر مقسوم ) اسلئے کہ یہ ابتداء کے اعتبار سے ہبہ ہے اور ہم اس کو کتاب الہبہ کے اندر بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ عوض عقد کے اندر مشروط نہ ہو ۔ اسلئے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک مطلق ہبہ ہے مگر تحقیق مکہ اس گھر کا عوض دے دیا گیا پس رجوع ممتنع ہو گیا۔ تشریح ہبہ کے اندر چونکہ مبادلہ مالی اور بیع کے معنی نہیں پائے جاتے۔ لہذا اگر کسی نے زید کو اپنا گھر ہبہ کر دیا تو کسی کوشفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔ البتہ اگر ہبہ بشرط العوض ہو تو اس کے اندر شفعہ ملے گا۔ مثلاً زید نے خالد کو اپنا گھر ہبہ کر دیا اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ خالد زید کو ایک ہزار روپے ہبہ کرے گا تو ہبہ بشرط العوض ہے اور اس کو ہبہ اور بیچ دونوں کا درجہ دیا جائے گا یعنی کہا جائے گا کہ یہ عقد ابتداء کے اعتبار سے ہبہ ہے اور نتہا کے اعتبار سے بیج ہے اور اس کے اندر دونوں کا لحاظ کیا جائے گا یعنی مبدے کا بھی اور منتہا کا بھی ۔ لہذا جب یہ مبدے کے اعتبار سے ہند ہوا تو اس پر ہبہ کے احکام جاری ہوں گے۔ اور ہبہ کے اندر قبضہ شرط ہے اور یہ شرط ہے کہ موہوب اور اس کا عوض دونوں قسمت شدہ ہوں شائع نہ ہوں۔ لہذا ان دونوں شرطوں کا یہاں بھی پایا جانا ضروری ہے اور چونکہ یہ منتہا کے اعتبار سے بیج ہے لہذا اس پر بیع کا حکم جاری ہوگا اور شفعہ ثابت ہو گا اس کو صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم اس کو کتاب الہبہ ۲۷۵ ج ۳ پر بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
ہاں اگر ہبہ کر دیا گیا مگر عقد کے اندر عوض کی شرط نہیں لگائی گئی اور بعد میں موہوب لڑ نے واہب کو اس کا عوض دے دیا تو اب یہ مطلق ہبہ ہے اور اس کے اندر شفعہ جاری نہ ہوگا نہ موہوب میں اور نہ عوض میں کیونکہ یہ دونوں تھے تو ہبہ ہی، مگر اتنی بات ہے کہ موہوب لڑنے اس کا عوض دے دیا تا کہ واہب رجوع نہ کر سکے۔ اس لئے کہ عوض دینے کی صورت میں ہبہ کے اندر رجوع باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ تفصیل کیلئے دیکھئے ہدایہ ص ۲۷۳ ج ۳۔
A note: The meaning of 'salaha 'anha' is that there is a dispute about the house and a settlement is made by giving something else. The meaning of 'salaha 'alayha' is that the house itself is given in the settlement. Upon this, the author of Hidayah said that in most copies of Quduri, the phrase is 'aw yusalihu 'alayha', whereas it should be 'aw yusalihu 'anha', otherwise the nature of the issue will change, as is evident. Is there a right of shuf'ah in gifted land or not? He (Imam Quduri) said: There is no shuf'ah in a gift for the reason we have mentioned, unless it is with a stipulated compensation, because it is a sale in its finality. Possession is necessary, and the gifted object and its compensation must not be undivided (sha'i'), because it is a gift in its inception. We have explained this in the Book of Gifts. Unlike the case where the compensation is not stipulated in the contract, because each of them is an absolute gift, but the recipient has indeed given compensation for the house, so revocation is prevented. Explanation: Since a gift does not involve financial exchange and the meaning of a sale, if someone gives his house as a gift to Zayd, no one will have shuf'ah. However, if it is a gift with a condition of compensation, then shuf'ah will be established. For example, Zayd gave his house to Khalid as a gift with the condition that Khalid gift Zayd one thousand rupees. This is a gift with stipulated compensation. It is given the status of both a gift and a sale: it is a gift in its inception and a sale in its finality, and both aspects are considered. Thus, when it is a gift in its inception, the rulings of gift apply: possession is required, and both the gifted object and its compensation must be divided (not undivided). When it is a sale in its finality, the ruling of sale applies and shuf'ah is established. The author of Hidayah says we have explained this in the Book of Gifts (vol. 3, p. 275). If a gift is made without a stipulation of compensation, and later the recipient gives the donor some compensation, then this is an absolute gift, and shuf'ah does not apply to either the gifted object or the compensation because both were gifts. However, the recipient gave compensation so that the donor cannot revoke the gift, because in case of compensation, revocation becomes invalid. For details, see Hidayah vol. 3, p. 273.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation on the right of shuf'ah (pre-emption) in the context of hibah (gift). The author begins with a textual note clarifying a critical variant in Quduri's matn: the phrase 'salaha 'anha' versus 'salaha 'alayha', which changes the legal implication of the settlement. Then, the main ruling is presented: no shuf'ah in a pure gift because it lacks the financial exchange characteristic of a sale. However, if the gift is conditional on compensation (hibah bi-shart al-'iwad), it is treated as a sale in its finality, thus shuf'ah is established. The reasoning is that such a transaction combines elements of gift (inception) and sale (end), so both sets of rules apply. For a valid shuf'ah claim, possession (qabd) is required, and both the gifted property and the compensation must be divided (not undivided shares). This is because the initial phase is a gift, which requires these conditions. If no condition of compensation is stipulated but compensation is given later, the transaction remains a pure gift and no shuf'ah arises; the compensation only prevents the donor from revoking the gift. The commentary follows the author's order: first the matn and its translation, then a detailed explanation with examples. The example of Zayd and Khalid illustrates the dual nature of a conditional gift. The authority of this ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah as transmitted by Imam Quduri and commented upon by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): Pre-emption right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold property before outsiders.
هبة بشرط العوض (hibah bi-shart al-'iwad): A gift where the donee is required to give something in return, making it akin to a sale in legal effect.
قبض (qabd): Physical or legal possession; a condition for validity of hibah and for transfer of ownership in sale.
شائع (sha'i'): Undivided share in a common property; a condition that the gifted property and its compensation must not be undivided for shuf'ah to apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a hibah bi-shart al-'iwad, why does shuf'ah apply according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because it is a pure gift and gifts always give shuf'ah.
B) Because it is treated as a sale in its finality, so the rules of sale apply.
C) Because the condition of compensation makes it a sale from the beginning.
D) Because shuf'ah applies to all property transfers regardless of the contract type.

Key Takeaway
Hibah bi-shart al-'iwad is a hybrid contract: it is a gift in essence but a sale in effect, so shuf'ah applies.

Shuf'ah When the Seller Has Khiyar al-Shart
Ruling on shuf'ah with seller's khiyar and timing of demand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shuf'ah when the seller has stipulated khiyar al-shart and identify when the shafi' must make the demand (talab).

Core Idea
Shuf'ah depends on actual transfer of ownership; seller's option blocks it until dropped.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in pre-emption (shuf'ah): a property sold with a stipulation that the seller retains an option to cancel (khiyar al-shart). The key question is when does the right of shuf'ah arise? The answer hinges on ownership transfer. We will also address a dispute among Hanafi scholars regarding the timing of the shafi' demand.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties' rights
The seller sells a house with a condition that he has the option (khiyar) to cancel within a specified period. The buyer and the shafi' (neighbor/partner with pre-emption right) await ownership transfer.
This is a common scenario: seller wants flexibility, but shafi' wants to exercise pre-emption.
2
State the general ruling
While the seller has the option, the property remains in his ownership. Hence, there is no shuf'ah because ownership has not yet transferred to the buyer.
Ownership is a prerequisite for shuf'ah.
3
Identify when shuf'ah becomes obligatory
When the seller drops the option (either by explicit cancellation or expiry), ownership transfers. At that moment, shuf'ah becomes wajib (obligatory) for the shafi' to claim.
The sale becomes a cause (sabab) for shuf'ah only upon dropping the option.
4
Determine the correct timing of the demand (talab)
The shafi' must make his demand (talab) at the time the seller drops the option, not at the time of the initial sale contract. Demand before that is futile because the cause was not yet realized.
Some earlier scholars (mashayikh) held that demand at sale suffices, but the correct view (mufta bihi) is at dropping the option.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and the tarjih
The author of Hidayah (al-Marghinani) explicitly rejects the earlier view and confirms the sahih qawl. The fatwa today follows this opinion.
This illustrates how later Hanafi masters settled a conflict between principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن باع بشرط الخيار فلا شفعة للشفيع لانه يمنع زوال الملك عن البائع فان اسقط الخيار وجبت الشفعة لانه زال المانع عن الزوال ويشترط الطلب عند سقوط الخيار في الصحيح لان البيع يصير سببا لزوال الملک عند ذالک ترجمہ ما مقدوری نے کہا اور جس نے بچا خیار کی شرط کے ساتھ تو شفیع کیلئے شفعہ نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ یہ خیار بائع ) روکتا ہے بالغ کی ملک کے زوال کو ۔ پس اگر بائع نے خیار ساقط کر دیا تو شفعہ ثابت ہو گا اسلئے کہ وہ چیز زائل ہوگئی جو زوال ملک کو روکنے والی تھی اور طلب شرط ہے۔ صحیح قول کے مطابق خیار کے سقوط کے وقت اسلئے کہ بیع سبب بنتی ہے زوال ملک کا اس وقت ( سقوط خیار کے وقت )۔ تشریح ہدایہ ص ۱۴ ج ۳ پر آپ پڑھ چکے کہ اگر بائع کو خیار ہو تو مبیع بائع کی ملکیت سے خارج نہ ہوگی ۔ اور اگر مشتری کو خیار ہوتو مبیع بائع کی ملکیت سے نکل جائے گی ۔ پھر مشتری کی ملکیت میں آئے گی یا نہیں اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے۔ بہر حال جب یہ تفصیل معلوم ہے تو اب سنئے ، بائع نے کوئی گھر فروخت کیا اور اپنے لئے خیار کی شرط لگالی تو چونکہ مبیع بائع کی ملکیت میں ہے تو ابھی شفیع کو حق شفعہ نہیں پہنچے گا۔ ہاں جب بائع خیار کو ساقط کر دے اور بیع کو نافذ کر دے تو جو چیز مانع تھی وہ زائل ہوگئی اور بیع بائع کی ملکیت سے نکل گئی تو اب شفیع کو شفعہ ملے گا۔ سوال اب رہا یہ مسئلہ کہ شفعہ کی طلب کس وقت شرط ہے؟ جواب تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر چہ بعض مشائخ نے وجود شرط شفعہ کا خیال کرتے ہوئے یوں کہا ہے کہ بوقت بیع طلب شرط ہے۔ مگر صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ قول صحیح نہیں بلکہ صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ طلب اس وقت شرط ہے جبکہ بائع خیار کو ساقط کر دے۔ کیونکہ جب بائع خیار کو ساقط کر دے گا اس وقت یہ بیع شفعہ کا سبب بنے گی ۔ لہذا تحقق سبب سے پہلے طلب لغو ہے۔
He (Imam Quduri) said: Whoever sells with a condition of option (khiyar), there is no shuf'ah for the shafi' (pre-emptor) because it prevents the transfer of ownership from the seller. If the seller drops the option, shuf'ah becomes obligatory because the obstacle to transfer has been removed. The demand (talab) is required at the time of dropping the option in the correct view, because the sale becomes a cause for transfer of ownership at that time. Translation: Imam Quduri said: Whoever sells with a condition of option, there is no shuf'ah for the shafi' because this option prevents the transfer of ownership from the seller. So if the seller drops the option, shuf'ah is established because the thing that prevented the transfer of ownership is removed. The demand is a condition in the correct view at the time of dropping the option, because the sale becomes a cause for transfer of ownership at that time. Explanation: You have read in Hidayah vol. 3, p. 14 that if the seller has an option, the sold property does not leave the seller's ownership. If the buyer has an option, the sold property leaves the seller's ownership. Then whether it enters the buyer's ownership or not, there is a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn). In any case, now listen: If a seller sells a house and stipulates an option for himself, since the sold property remains in the seller's ownership, the shafi' does not yet have the right of shuf'ah. But when the seller drops the option and confirms the sale, the obstacle is removed and the sale exits the seller's ownership, so now the shafi' gets shuf'ah. The remaining question is: when is the demand required? The answer is: although some mashayikh have said, considering the existence of the condition of shuf'ah, that the demand is required at the time of sale, the author of Hidayah says this is not correct. Rather, the correct view is that the demand is required when the seller drops the option, because at that time the sale becomes a cause for shuf'ah. Therefore, demand before the cause is realized is futile.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on shuf'ah when the seller has stipulated a khiyar al-shart (option condition) in the sale contract. The key principle is that shuf'ah depends on the transfer of ownership from the seller to the buyer. If the seller has an option, ownership does not transfer until the option is dropped. Hence, no shuf'ah while the option subsists. When the seller drops the option, ownership transfers, and shuf'ah becomes operative. The commentary then addresses a subsidiary issue: when must the shafi' make the demand (talab)? Some earlier scholars held that demand must be made at the time of the contract because shuf'ah is based on the contract. However, the correct view (as per the author of Hidayah) is that demand must be made when the seller drops the option, because the sale only becomes a cause (sabab) for shuf'ah at that moment. Demand before that is futile. The passage also references a prior discussion in Hidayah about the effect of khiyar on ownership: if the seller has khiyar, the property does not leave his ownership; if the buyer has khiyar, it does leave the seller's ownership (though entry into buyer's ownership is disputed between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn). The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, and the correct view (mufta bihi) is as articulated by al-Marghinani.

Key Terms
خیار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulated option in a sale contract allowing one party to cancel the contract within a specified period.
طلب (talab): The demand made by the shafi' to claim shuf'ah; a necessary step to establish the right.
سبب (sabab): Cause; the sale becomes the cause (sabab) for shuf'ah only when ownership is actually transferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When must the shafi' make the demand (talab) for shuf'ah if the seller has a khiyar al-shart?
A) At the time of the sale contract.
B) At the time when the seller drops the option.
C) Within three days of the contract.
D) Immediately after the option period expires.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, shuf'ah arises only upon actual transfer of ownership; a seller's option delays it until dropped, and the shafi' must make demand at that moment.

Shuf'ah When Buyer Has Khiyar al-Shart
Ruling on shuf'ah when buyer has option condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that shuf'ah is established immediately when the buyer has an option condition and distinguish the treatment from khiyar al-ru'yah.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is established upon contract even with buyer's option; shafi' has no option and his taking is acceptance.

This lesson examines a nuanced fiqh issue: when a property is sold with a condition of option (khiyar al-shart) for the buyer, does the right of preemption (shuf'ah) arise immediately? The Hanafi position, based on consensus that ownership transfers from the seller, affirms shuf'ah. We will break down the reasoning and its corollaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the sale of a property with a condition of option for the buyer. The ruling is that shuf'ah is established immediately upon the contract.
This is stated explicitly in the first sentence of the passage.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the consensus (ittifaq) that the option does not prevent the transfer of ownership from the seller. Shuf'ah is based on ownership transfer.
The text says 'because it does not prevent the transfer of ownership from the seller by consensus'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The underlying reasoning: Shuf'ah is a right that arises from joint ownership or adjacency, which depends on ownership. Since ownership transfers from seller to buyer at the moment of contract, the conditions for shuf'ah are satisfied regardless of the option.
This is the link between the consensus and the ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text implies that other schools may disagree, but the Hanafi position is based on the consensus. The passage also references an 'objection' concerning the buyer's right to shuf'ah if he has an option, which was clarified elsewhere.
The cross-madhhab status is 'mukhtalaf fih' as per the source.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position as stated is the mufta bihi (operative ruling). The shafi' has no option, and his taking the property within three days makes the sale binding. Khiyar al-ru'yah is not nullified by implication.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اشترى بشرط الخيار وجبت الشفعة لانه لا يمنع زوال الملك عن البائع بالاتفاق والشفعة تبتنى عليه علی مامر واذا اخذها فى الثلث وجب البيع لعجز المشترى عن الرد ولاخيار للشفيع لانه يثبت بالشرط وهو للمشترى دون الشفيع وان بيعت دار الى جنبها والخيار لاحدهما فله الاخذ بالشفعة اما للبائع فظاهر البقاء ملكه فى التي يشفع بها وكذا اذا كان للمشترى وفيه اشكال اوضحناه في البيوع فلا نعيده واذا اخذها كان اجازة منه للبيع بخلاف ما اذا اشتراها ولم يرها حيث لا يبطل خياره باخذ ما بيع بجنبها بالشفعة لان خيار الروية لا يبطل بصريح الأبطال فكيف بدلالته ثم اذا حضر شفيع الدار الاولى له ان ياخذها دون الثانية لانعدام ملكه فى الاولى حين بيعت الثانية. ترجمہ اور اگر مشترکی نے خیار کی شرط کے ساتھ خریدا تو شفعہ ثبات ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہتی بالاتفاق بائع سے ملک کے زوال کو نہیں روکتا اور شفعہ گذشتہ تفصیل کے مطابق اسی پر مبنی ہے اور جبکہ شفیع نے گھر کو تین دن کے اندر اندر لے لیا تو بیع لازم ہوگئی مشتری کے رد سے عاجز ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اور شفیع کیلئے خیار نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ خیار شرط سے ثابت ہوتا ہے اور یہ مشتری کیلئے ہے نہ کہ شفیع کیلئے اور اگر اس دار کے پہلو میں کوئی گھر فروخت کیا گیا اور خیار ان دونوں میں سے کسی کیلئے ہے تو اس کیلئے شفعہ ہے۔ بہر حال بائع کیلئے تو ظاہر ہے۔ اس کی ملکیت کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے اس گھر کے اندر جس کے ذریعہ وہ شفعہ لے رہا ہے اور ایسے ہی جبکہ مشتری کیلئے ہو اور اس میں ایک اشکال ہے جسے ہم کتاب البیوع میں واضح کر چکے ہیں اسے دہرانہے کی ضرورت نہیں۔ اور جب شفیع نے اسے لے لیا تو یہ اس کی طرف سے بیع کی اجازت ہے بخلاف اس صورت کے جب اس نے اسے خریدا اور اسے نہیں دیکھا تو اس کا خیار اس کے شفعہ لے لینے سے باطل نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ خیار الرویہ صریح ابطال سے بھی باطل نہیں ہوتا تو دلالت سے کیسے باطل ہوگا۔ پھر جب پہلے گھر کا شفیع حاضر ہو تو اسے پہلے گھر کو لینے کا حق ہے دوسرے گھر کو نہیں اسلئے کہ جب دوسرا گھر بیچا گیا اس وقت اس کی پہلے گھر میں ملک نہیں تھی۔
And if someone purchases with a condition of option, shuf'ah becomes established because it (the option) does not prevent the transfer of ownership from the seller by consensus, and shuf'ah is based upon that as previously mentioned. And if the shafi' takes it within three days, the sale becomes binding because the buyer becomes unable to return (the property), and the shafi' has no option because the option is established by stipulation and belongs to the buyer, not the shafi'. And if a house adjacent to it is sold and the option belongs to one of them (the seller or buyer of the adjacent house), then that person has the right of shuf'ah. For the seller, it is obvious because his ownership in the property through which he claims shuf'ah remains. Similarly if the option belongs to the buyer, but there is an objection that we have clarified in the Book of Sales, so we do not repeat it. And when he (the shafi') takes it, it becomes his acceptance of the sale. Unlike the case where he purchased it without seeing it, his option (of inspection) is not nullified by taking the adjacent property through shuf'ah, because khiyar al-ru'yah is not nullified by explicit annulment, so how could it be by implication? Then, if the shafi' of the first house is present, he has the right to take the first house, not the second, because at the time the second was sold, he had no ownership in the first. Translation: And if the buyer purchases with a condition of option, shuf'ah is established because it (the option) does not prevent the transfer of ownership from the seller by consensus, and shuf'ah is based upon that as per previous detail. And when the shafi' takes the house within three days, the sale becomes binding due to the buyer's inability to return, and the shafi' has no option because the option is established by stipulation and is for the buyer, not the shafi'. And if a house adjacent to this house is sold and the option is for one of them (seller or buyer), then that person has the right of shuf'ah. For the seller it is obvious due to his remaining ownership in the house through which he is claiming shuf'ah. Similarly when it is for the buyer, there is an objection which we have clarified in the Book of Sales, so no need to repeat. And when the shafi' takes it, it is his permission of the sale. Unlike the case where he purchased it without seeing it, his option (of inspection) is not nullified by his taking the adjacent property through shuf'ah, because khiyar al-ru'yah is not nullified by explicit annulment, so how could it be by implication? Then, when the shafi' of the first house is present, he has the right to take the first house, not the second, because at the time the second was sold, he had no ownership in the first.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on shuf'ah when the buyer has a khiyar al-shart. Key difference from the seller's khiyar: the buyer's option does not prevent the transfer of ownership from the seller by consensus. Hence, shuf'ah is established immediately upon the contract. The text then explains several corollaries: (1) If the shafi' takes possession within three days (the usual option period), the sale becomes binding on the buyer (who cannot cancel). (2) The shafi' does not get the option (khiyar al-shart) because it belongs exclusively to the buyer. (3) If two adjacent properties are sold, and one seller or buyer has an option, that person can claim shuf'ah in the other property. The seller's claim is straightforward; the buyer's claim has a subtle issue (referred to Book of Sales). (4) When the shafi' takes the property, it is considered an acceptance of the sale by the shafi', but this does not affect the buyer's khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection) if the buyer had not seen the property. This is because khiyar al-ru'yah is a strong right that cannot be nullified even by explicit annulment, so implied actions like taking shuf'ah do not nullify it. (5) Priority: if a shafi' of the first (adjacent) property presents, he takes the first property only, not the second, because when the second was sold, he had no ownership in the first (i.e., he was not yet a co-owner of the second property). The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, with the mufta bihi position as stated.

Key Terms
خیار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option or right to cancel a contract that is stipulated as a condition at the time of the contract.
خیار الرویہ (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option of inspection; a buyer who purchases without seeing the property has the right to cancel upon inspection.
اجازت (ijazah): Permission or ratification; shafi's taking the property is considered his approval of the sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What effect does the shafi's taking of the property through shuf'ah have on the buyer's khiyar al-ru'yah if the buyer had not seen the property?
A) It nullifies the khiyar al-ru'yah because the shafi's action implies acceptance.
B) It does not nullify the khiyar al-ru'yah because it is a strong right not nullified by implication.
C) It only nullifies the khiyar if the shafi took possession within three days.
D) The buyer loses the khiyar al-ru'yah once the shafi claims shuf'ah.

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah is established immediately upon a sale with buyer's option, the shafi' has no option, and his taking constitutes acceptance; khiyar al-ru'yah remains unaffected.

Effect of Buyer's Option on Shuf'a: Waiver of Khiyar al-Shart, Not Khiyar al-Ru'ya
Ruling on khiyar and shuf'a interaction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the effects of khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ru'ya on shuf'a and apply the appropriate ruling.

Core Idea
Taking shuf'a voids the buyer's khiyar al-shart but not khiyar al-ru'ya; the shafi' does not inherit the option.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies how the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) interacts with different types of buyer's options. Understanding when an option is waived and when it persists is essential for correctly applying shuf'a rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two option types
Recognize that the buyer may have either khiyar al-shart (a stipulated option, typically three days) or khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection for unseen goods). Each has different rules.
Khiyar al-shart is contractual; khiyar al-ru'ya is based on lack of sight.
2
Apply the general rule for khiyar al-shart
When a buyer with khiyar al-shart takes the adjacent property via shuf'a, this act constitutes implicit permission for the sale, making it binding and waiving the option.
The buyer's action indicates consent to the sale.
3
Recognize the exception for khiyar al-ru'ya
Khiyar al-ru'ya is not voided by mere implication; it remains intact unless the buyer explicitly renounces it. Taking shuf'a does not imply renunciation of inspection rights.
The text states: 'The option of inspection is not voided by explicit annulment, so how can it be voided by implication?'
4
Determine the shafi's position
The shafi' (pre-emptor) does not inherit the buyer's option because khiyar al-shart is a contractual right between the original seller and buyer only.
The option is not transferable to a third party.
